Free Talk

Not Removing the Courtyard Grass Studio: Miscellaneous Talks

Learning Half a Cavendish 172

Sir Henry Cavendish, an Englishman, was born in 1731 and died in 1810. This Double Tenth Day marks the bicentennial of his birth.

He was a wealthy scientist, a scientist with wealth.

He discovered hydrogen gas in 1766, calling it "Inflammable Air"; in 1784, he proved that water is formed by the explosion of inflammable air and one-fifth of common air, with that one-fifth being the oxygen that Lavoisier named. In 1798, he determined the specific gravity of the earth, allowing us to know its immense weight without having to weigh the entire planet. He had many inventions; these are his primary contributions.

Although Cavendish made significant academic contributions, he was inherently solitary and antisocial, especially disliking the company of women. If he happened to see a female servant in his home, she would invariably be dismissed. In his later years, when someone hosted a banquet to honor his contributions, he escaped through the back door. Upon his death, he dismissed his only servant, so he could leave the world alone and unburdened.

He often kept his scientific experiments secret. Fifty years after his death, his notes were finally published. Thus, the words "Cavendish" and "Selfish" became associated. Selfish scientists have since had an archetype, using Cavendish as a shield. They have learned half of Cavendish, actually learning the worse half while forgetting the better. They only care about climbing the tree of science, picking the ripe fruit for themselves, and throwing the peel and seeds down. They don't care whether the brothers at the bottom of the tree can eat or not. They have learned Cavendish's reclusiveness and selfishness while forgetting his efforts towards great inventions.

After Cavendish's death, Berthelot said: (Chemistry is a French science, and its founder Lavoisier is immortal). Sir Ed. Thorpe retorted: (Chemistry is an English science, and its founder Cavendish is immortal). If the aloof Cavendish had a spirit, he would surely laugh at Berthelot and Thorpe's pointlessness.

Recording Old Feelings About Decaying Lotus Flowers 173

— Jing Mengdie

The gentlemen and ladies of Xicheng, during the height of summer, all consider drinking tea in the park the only pastime. The deep shade provides refuge from the scorching sun. The narrow, noisy and dusty city finds a haven of coolness there. I especially love the area around Hanbi Bridge. The pond has lotus flowers, and whenever they are in bloom, I lean on the railing, enjoying the view of the water. I often stay until late at night. I remember a line: ("Ten thousand round pearls run across the jade plate; a pond of shattered moon covers the flower's shadow.") The beauty of the scene is imaginable. This summer, when the pond's lotus flowers bloomed profusely, it was during a time of widespread flooding. There were few visitors, which was a shame. Moreover, I was briefly away for two weeks. Autumn rain covers Maoling, and Xiangru is already ill. Fallen flowers cover the lake, and Du Mu arrives late. Returning to Liangxi, just after getting off the train, I immediately went to the park to see them. I only saw the lush lotus leaves, with the fish still playing east and west. The flowers, except for three or five standing tall, had their pollen and beauty fallen, leaving their marks on the water. The fragrant red lotus is gone, and the person in the blue shirt is old. Another year has easily passed, and it is autumn wind again. Only facing these understanding famous flowers, I compose a short poem of sorrow. Thus, there is a regulated verse about decaying lotus flowers: The lotus picking song ends, and the heat initially recedes; red and green scatter, evoking old travels. The fallen flowers have never returned to the murky mud; the withered branches still entrust themselves to the clear stream. Having experienced wind, rain, heat, and cold, lying in the rivers and lakes, the scenery is autumnal. In the blink of an eye, prosperity becomes flowing water; even the old mandarin ducks are full of sorrow.

An Interview with a Shanghai Miss (Part 2) 174

— Mo Yi

▲ Her Daily Life

Furthermore, she loves music. This is the influence her father had on her, because her father was the leader of the Petrograd Symphony Orchestra. She is proficient in piano. Jazz music is also one of her loves. So, every day after 4 p.m., people passing by her house can often hear the resounding and pleasing sound of the piano. Helen told the reporter, ("Dancing is also one of my favorite sports. I dance almost every night.") Indeed, she is proud. In the dance hall, she is often praised for how graceful her dancing posture is. She also loves swimming, ice skating, riding horses, and driving cars. She said confidently, ("I can drive the car as fast as lightning.") Her daily life is roughly as follows: She gets up at 7:30 in the morning. After breakfast, she drives herself to school. She studies business. She often goes home for lunch. After returning home from school at 4 p.m., she practices the piano or reads until dinner. Because she likes to eat early, she has dinner at 7 p.m. After dinner, she goes to see a movie, or goes dancing, or strolls along Avenue Joffre with friends.

▲ The Seven-Hour Sleep System

Helen said, ("I think seven hours of sleep is enough for a girl.") Although she talks like this, during summer vacation, she often sleeps for about ten or eleven hours. She has very few friends. She said she only has one girlfriend, named Lei Tailu Pengwei, who is her friendly neighbor. Helen's mother grew up in Crimea. She was already known for her beauty in her hometown at the age of seventeen. Her father was a native of Petrograd. When it comes to the secrets of beauty, Helen said she has none, but she pays close attention to her health and diet. According to her, she has never reduced her food intake like American movie stars.

▲ A Lover of Sour and Spicy Foods

The reporter asked, ("What kind of food does the lady like to eat?") She seemed to understand that this question was related to her beauty, so she casually replied, ("Sour and spicy food.") The reporter couldn't help but say in surprise, following her, ("Sour and spicy food?") ("That's right. Sour and spicy food.") she replied to me in a musical voice. She has never drunk milk or eaten eggs. Meat seems to be one of her favorite foods.

▲ The Dragon is Not Meant to be in a Pond

The reporter asked, ("Has the lady ever participated in the beauty contest?") ("No. This is the first time many people have said that I am a child. But I am confident. I am not a child in any way.") She said that she has the extravagant hope of going on stage, but she is unwilling to bury herself in a Shanghai that is as big as a house. She wants to go to Hollywood and New York to develop her acting talent. She does not smoke, but sometimes she drinks some champagne. In short, Ms. Helen is a beautiful and young girl. In addition to her existing gorgeous clothes, her parents' love, the huge amount of money for her to spend, one or two cars, and seeking pleasure in the dance hall, she needs music and a young husband, as she herself said, to make her life more fulfilling.

World Miscellany 175

▲ The Busiest Woman in London

Miss Phyllis Gordon, a Scottish girl, is only twenty-two years old this year. She has extremely beautiful features. She works thirteen hours a day, dances six hours, and sleeps four hours. The rest of the time is spent on three meals a day. She has now jumped to become a director of a London hotel company, completely managing the busiest hotel and bearing heavy responsibilities. This lady can be regarded as the busiest woman in London. The general working women in our country are probably envious of her.

▲ A Four-Year-Old Piano Expert

In North-umberland, England, there is a miner named Sherrington. He has a son named Sidney, who is only four years old, but already plays the piano well. His ten fingers land on the keys, making a sound like large and small pearls falling on a jade plate. Professor Stafford, a music expert from Sudland, conducted a rigorous examination of him and sighed at his rare talent. Perhaps he will shake the world in the future. (Haik)

Anecdotes from the Neighborhood 176

— Qi Yun

Next door lives a Cantonese family. The third floor is rented by a lady from Wuxia. Her movements seem quite secretive. She goes out at night and returns in the morning light. The sound of her knocking on the door always disturbs my sweet dreams. My family all look down on her, saying that this lady is immersed in the city's nightlife and is probably like the "Vamp" described in Western stories. I also thought so. Therefore, I had a curious desire to spy on where she goes at night. But after a long time, I couldn't find out, and gradually I put it aside.

One night, I was out with a friend and entered a certain dance hall. Across from us was a dance partner, who was the lady from next door. I told my friend about it, and we got up and danced with her. Her posture was graceful and charming. Asking her name, it was Zhu Lilin.

After a long time, I became familiar with Lilin. Lilin gradually told me about her life experiences, often sobbing. She had experienced the vicissitudes of life. She said, ("A good husband, how can one look up to him for life? When a woman is unmarried, she is like a bird in the forest, free to protect herself with innocence. Once married, she is like a phoenix in a cage. Those who are lucky become playthings for self-comfort, while those who are unlucky are worn down and killed. I married at sixteen. My husband initially treated me well, but then he was seduced by a wanton woman and heartlessly abandoned me. Helplessly, I remarried, for the sake of life. But fate is often perverse, and I sighed even more at marrying the wrong person. Soon after, I remarried, but it was in vain. Now I work in the dance industry. It is not what I want, but I have no choice.")

Her story is ordinary and unremarkable, but it is an ancient and modern tragedy that beauty is fleeting. In the brightly lit and wine-filled places, even with the extreme pleasure of jade smiles and pearl fragrances, many people have sleeves full of tears or secretly wipe away tears.

I remembered that Ms. Shi Huangsun once had a good film (The Love History of a Female Singer), which depicts the romance and pain of a female singer in every detail. Therefore, I thought that the encounters of dance hall girls, if someone could depict them well, would have a thousand times more strangeness, whether it is romance or pain. Why is today's so-called sound song and dance film in the West so uniform, only using the dance hall's prosperity and splendor as superficial decorations?

Recently, I learned that the Minzhong Guosheng Sound Film Company produced a film (Such is Paradise). Its special feature lies in its unique and poignant depiction beyond prosperity and splendor. All the hidden pains of the family and the darkness of society can be seen through the transformation of a dancer, giving a very deep and vivid impression. In addition to the enjoyment of romance, the audience gets a very enthusiastic stimulus. I will invite Lilin to watch it, and she will probably have even more feelings of sympathy.

Rambling Talks at the "Looking at the Echo" Studio 177

— Gan Yi

Li Jingxi

After Yuan Shikai dissolved the parliament, he established a political conference, advocating the reorganization of various societies. Li Zhongxuan (Jingxi) was then a guest in the capital, actively seeking advancement. Shikai did not want to give him an important position but praised his eloquent talent, appointing him chairman of this conference. Jingxi was overjoyed, quite invigorated. After the conference ended, he was given the position of senator, which disappointed him. He often told people that his merits were not rewarded. He aspired to govern Sichuan and Guangdong. Shikai heard of this and summoned his son, Guojun, for an audience. Yang Xingcheng (Shiqi), the Left Vice-Minister of the Government Affairs Hall, also praised Guojun's talent and knowledge, saying he was capable of shouldering responsibilities. He was then appointed Governor of Guangdong. Guojun declined and was about to take up his new post when Xiangcheng told him: "Your father's spirit and talent are a hundred times better than mine. With time, when my term ends, the one who will inherit China will be no one else but him." Guojun replied yes, yes. He retired and told his father about it. Jingxi stamped his feet and said, "It's over." It was then that he realized that Shikai respected him but did not trust him. He then lived in seclusion in Xijin. It was rumored that Qian Gancheng (Nengxun), the Right Vice-Minister, was going to transfer Jingxi. He wrote a letter to Shiqi, saying that although he was old, his heart was still strong, and he was not accustomed to living in seclusion. He wished to assist the central government. Shiqi showed the letter to Shikai, implying that he was giving way to a worthy person. Shikai said, "Why is Zhong hesitant to leave?" Gancheng was also not allowed to leave him far away. He told Zhongxuan, "If it is appropriate, I will definitely rely on him." After a short while, Ding Zhenduo, the president of the Audit Court, died in office. Jingxi was appointed to replace him. The order stated (Li Zhaozhen will act as an agent before he takes office). Jingxi was in Tianjin and was about to go to Beijing to take office. Angered by Shikai's manipulation, he resigned from the post. From then until the end of Xiangcheng's term, he did not discuss political affairs. When Huangpi was in power, he was appointed to the Grand Secretariat. After only three days, he encountered a disaster and fled south in disarray. He died soon after. His fellow villager, Gong Xianzhou (Xinzhan), was then in charge of the interior, writing an article to ask the governing Duan to issue a decree to commend and honor him. Jingxi, Qirui, and Xinzhan were all from Hefei.

A Husband's Wife (10) 178

— Jiang Hongjiao

(I'm a fool? You're the fool. One always needs some integrity. Whoever is inferior should be assigned inferior tasks. Just now I wanted to advise Mr. Li, but your words stopped me. Am I still a fool?) Mr. Chen explained his reasoning.

(Aren't you a fool? Fool! Fool! I judge you to be a fool. What about it?)

(Then you're a silly woman!) Mr. Chen said with a comical attitude, mostly joking.

(You're a stupid thief!) Mrs. Chen lowered her face, genuinely scolding.

(Why are you scolding me?)

(Why shouldn't I scold you! Think about it yourself. Why do you have to meddle in other couples' affairs? If others know, they won't necessarily say you're a fool. Maybe they'll even say you're helping Lanzhen with ulterior motives.)

(Lanzhen is your friend. I'm helping her, partly because I pity her and partly because of your relationship. Don't get jealous and turn this into a big issue! With a fierce wife like you, how would a husband dare to move?)

Mr. Chen's explanation only made Mrs. Chen even more suspicious and ignited her anger. She sternly questioned Mr. Chen. Generally, if friends have occasional disagreements, a quarrel can be avoided if one party is tolerant. The stricter the criticism between husband and wife, the easier it is to cause conflict. So, they quarreled.

Mr. Chen did feel sorry for Lanzhen. At the same time, he thought about his wife's wasteful spending, not appreciating his hard work in earning money. He couldn't help but feel resentful. He had never expressed such resentment before, but now that he had such an opportunity, he vented it out. He couldn't stop himself.

(You suspect me. I can swear to God that my heart is more upright than anyone else's. Tell me, what have you seen or heard that makes you suspicious? But I trust you very much. Although you often play cards with Li Jingbo and go to dance halls together, sometimes you come home two or three hours late, if I wanted to suspect you of something improper, I could strictly interfere with you. Think for yourself. In these past few years, which thing have you considered for me? My socks are torn, and you don't mend them for me, but you buy silk stockings for yourself, each pair costing five and a half dollars. If you don't buy them, that's fine, but when you buy them, you always buy half a dozen at a time. How much do you spend on social expenses each month? I always go home by eight or nine o'clock at the latest every night. What about you?)

This street used cheap new japonica rice, and Song goods continued to arrive, and the sales market inevitably suffered squeezing, resulting in fewer transactions, and the market price was also short of angular allowance. ▲ New Zha got few heads and went to zero and scattered, with the top middle two grades being the most popular. There was a slight opening of foreign Lu tip and glutinous rice, and the price was still stable.

Zhejiang Province Autumn Cocoons Will Be Launched Next 192

Cocoons in Hangzhou and Shaoxing are expected to open scales tomorrow and the day after

This year, farmers in various counties of Hangzhou and Shaoxing provinces have been promoted by the officialdom to raise autumn silkworms, so they have all started early. The ant feeding was stimulated and smooth. The weather was very clear and warm at the beginning. The development after receiving the ants was quite good. During the three sleeps, there was a big wind and rain, followed by a big flood. The local silkworm councils hatched in various villages were severely damaged. Recently, the early gang is on the cocoon, and the late gang is Wang Ye during the big sleep, and the continuous rain is cold, and most of the silkworm ants have found white zombies, and there are occasional soft and unresponsive ones. This year, the autumn cocoon harvest in Zhejiang Province is at most five or six points. The new cocoons will be launched next. The Hangzhou and Shaoxing cocoon firms are expected to open the scale tomorrow and the day after.

Youth Garden

Snake Swallows Wolf 217

— Wen Qing

I used to hear that natives in the tropics catch live snakes in their hands, bite off their heads in one bite, then bite them off section by section, slowly swallowing them, with a taste like we have when eating sugarcane and sweet rice stalks. After I arrived in a country below the equator, I really wanted to see them enjoying this kind of tasty delicacy, but I never saw it once. Perhaps it's because I didn't go to visit deep in the mountains and valleys.

Originally, in the tropics, news of people eating snakes and snakes eating people could often be heard. Even the shepherds and woodcutters near volcanoes sometimes went out in the morning and never returned in the evening. Some people said they were eaten by tigers, others said they were eaten by snakes. According to experienced hunters with knowledge of animal behavior, if a tiger eats a person, human hands and feet can be found in the forest or on the hillside, because tigers eat people but don't eat hands and feet, just as people eat chicken eggs but don't eat eggshells. Based on this formula, it can be inferred that those people were eaten by snakes. But I always had some disbelief. How could such a long body and small head and neck swallow a person? Because the snakes I often saw on the roads lined with tall green trees, green branches, and fresh grass were just big snakes. There were long ones, short ones, thick ones, thin ones, blue, red, purple, green, all sorts of colors of snakes, flattened by the洋鬼子's cars, sleeping on the road with blurred bloodstains. The street cleaners in red vests dragged the snakes, one by one, like dead eels, to the garbage bin every morning. It can be imagined that there are many snakes in the tropics.

One day, a friend who grew up in the tropics was talking to me about hygiene issues. I always felt that the natives were not very particular about hygiene. No, it was the same for some of the overseas Chinese. They liked to sleep on damp ground and liked to eat stale meat, so they were often prone to illness, and people died more frequently and quickly. Diseases enter through the mouth. First and foremost, I advocate eating fresh things.

(In the tropics, to avoid the occurrence of strange diseases, it is not advisable to eat too much meat and fish. If you must eat it, you should eat fresh and lively ones.)

(Can you eat live animals? Unless you are a snake.)

(Of course, they are killed and cooked thoroughly, and eaten when they are fragrant. Don't snakes also kill animals and eat them?)

(Yes, snakes swallow animals whole and alive. It seems you are still not as hygienic as a snake.)

Tree Shade 218

— Bing She

"How do you know that snakes swallow live animals?"

(My aunt's family lives by hunting. I don't know how many wild animals they have at home now. A week ago, my uncle caught a big snake on a high mountain next to a volcano. It was as thick as a water bucket and more than fifty feet long. He was going to sell it to the zoo. It is still in a sturdy iron cage. It has a large appetite and eats two wild boars and one wolf every day. One day, my cousin killed a deer on the mountain, dragged it back, and put it in the cage to feed it. Not only did it not eat it, but it was very angry. It twisted its tail and knocked the dead deer into the corner of the iron cage. If a live animal is put in, it will wag its head and tail to show how happy

Home
